<div id="review_144670310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144670310" />
    <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers"><img alt="TheBookSmugglers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316717753p2/1223249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144670310?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheBookSmugglers" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers">TheBookSmugglers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=women-in-scifi-fantasy-ya-and-mg">women-in-scifi-fantasy-ya-and-mg</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=best-of-2010">best-of-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144670310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16957553841048745236">Original Review <a href='http://thebooksmugglers.com/2010/03/book-review-incarceron-by-catherine-fisher.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE</a><br/><br/>Incarceron is a vast, encompassing prison. Instead of steel bars and cell blocks, however, Incarceron is a world in itself; it is a metal world where nothing is created nor wasted, where stars and sky are near forgotten fairy tales, where all live in a cutthroat world, fighting for food and survival. Even more than that, Incarceron is alive – it observes everything that goes on within its walls, it’s red seeing eye omnipresent to the mortals within. Incarceron is all they hav</span>
  <span id="freeText16957553841048745236" style="display:none">Original Review <a href="http://thebooksmugglers.com/2010/03/book-review-incarceron-by-catherine-fisher.html" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a><br /><br />Incarceron is a vast, encompassing prison. Instead of steel bars and cell blocks, however, Incarceron is a world in itself; it is a metal world where nothing is created nor wasted, where stars and sky are near forgotten fairy tales, where all live in a cutthroat world, fighting for food and survival. Even more than that, Incarceron is alive – it observes everything that goes on within its walls, it’s red seeing eye omnipresent to the mortals within. Incarceron is all they have ever known – although there is a myth about one man, a prophet named Sapphique, that was the only one able to escape to the mysterious outside.<br /><br />Finn is a child of Incarceron, remembering only when he woke up in a dark, squalid cell two years ago, mad with fear and lost memories. Now seventeen, Finn has been forced by circumstance to join a crew of “Scum” – that is, ruthless thieves and bandits, that call themselves the Comitatus. One day, Finn makes a shocking discovery – a crystal key, whose design matches the tattoo on Finn’s wrist. The key, which Finn and those around him believe could be the way out of Incarceron, also turns out to be a communication device, and Finn finds himself able to speak to a mysterious girl, named Claudia.<br /><br />On the outside of Incarceron, Claudia is the daughter of the Incarceron’s Warden, and set to marry the prince of the realm. Frustrated with her bleak future and the cutthroat political games in which she finds herself ensnared, Claudia is determined to prove that the monarchy is corrupt, and to find a way to instigate change in the static, innovation-fearing kingdom – and the way she plans to do this, is to discover Incarceron’s secrets. When she finds a crystal key in her father’s study, she finds a link to a world that is nothing like the ideal utopia that Incarceron was supposed to be – and she and Finn must work together to bring him out of Incarceron, and into the “real” world.<br /><br />And with Incarceron itself watching, waiting, and toying with its inhabitants, Claudia and Finn’s task is no small feat.<br /><br />Incarceron is an amazing feat of a novel from author Catherine Fisher. The book, actually initially published in the UK back in 2007, is part dystopian critique, part science fiction parable, part fantasy. This is not an easy blend to pull together, but Ms. Fisher does it with aplomb. Her world building in particular is PHENOMENAL. I loved the oddity of advanced technology in a royalty-imposed archaic time period – the monarchs and nobles emulate the late medieval western model of courts, down to the dress, castles and mannerisms. But this is not a medieval society! Claudia’s world has incredibly advanced technology, from “skin wands” to give humans the permanent appearance of youth to programable holograms, to artificial intelligence and reality-shifting tools. Despite this technology, however, those in power have resisted any change, abandoning their advanced tools in order to embrace the ways of old, in an attempt to control the population – which rings as very familiar. There’s also Incarceron itself, which is a whole new world on its own. Initially an experiment to create a perfect world for the unruly masses, of course went wrong. The concept of a utopia that is actually a dystopia isn’t really a new one, but this Ms. Fisher writes it so well, and with such awesome variation within Incarceron itself, of A.I. gone horribly awry, it hardly matters.<br /><br />In terms of plotting, Incarceron is also surefooted, as it packs in revelation upon revelation, surprises, and twists at an expert pace. I could not put Incarceron down – Ms. Fisher is one hell of a storyteller.<br /><br />Finally, what is a book without its characters? The cast of this novel is similarly well-rounded, though at first glance, they are very standard, fantasy archetypes. There’s the rebellious, intelligent (and beautiful) future queen; the orphaned boy thief with a heart of gold and a destiny to save the land; the calm, wise teacher; the jealous, handsome, morally-ambiguous best friend; the ragamuffin tag along girl; the zealous, prophecy-driven priest; the power-usurping, beautifully cruel queen; etc. These are very familiar character molds, no doubt about it – but as Incarceron progresses, the characters are shown in different ways. Not one thing is exactly how it seems, and that goes for characters as well. In particular, I loved the character of Claudia’s father – the cold, immutable, powerful Warden of Incarceron, Lord John Arlex. I loved the insights to his character throughout the book, especially in his strained relationship with Claudia’s tutor, Jared, and the Warden’s terrified – yet defiant – daughter, Claudia. (There’s one particular scene near the end of the book between these three characters that is made of mind-blowing awesomeness.)<br /><br />So far as protagonists go, Claudia is as plucky as they come, but it is Finn that captures hearts with his vision, his trusting friendships, and his courage. The other character I truly enjoyed is the morally ambiguous Keiro – handsome and power-hungry, different characters have different interpretations of Keiro. Finn, as his oath-brother, is tied to Keiro by an unbreakable bond – should one of them die, it is the other’s responsibility to avenge them at any cost. And, as a loyal friend, Finn knows Keiro’s flaws, his hunger for power, his recklessness, but he also believes that underneath it all, Keiro would do anything for Finn. Other characters, however, are not so generous, as Keiro is seen as a rogue, out only to use Finn to get him out of Incarceron, no matter the cost. In any case, Keiro is a character that isn’t easy to peg, and I’m excited to see what happens with him in the next book.<br /><br />With its breathtaking world-building, admirable characters, and exceptional plotting, Incarceron is a dystopian, sci-fi gem. I loved it, and I cannot wait for the next book in the series, Sapphique!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16957553841048745236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_78516520" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78516520" />
    <a title="oliviasbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks"><img alt="oliviasbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257619306p2/2843533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78516520?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="oliviasbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="oliviasbooks" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks">oliviasbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=scifi-dystopian-apocalyptic">scifi-dystopian-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=cliffhanger">cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=swapped-or-given-away">swapped-or-given-away</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=other-creatures">other-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=multiple-povs-letters-diaries">multiple-povs-letters-diaries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78516520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3389586978076639844">The prison Incarceron reminds me a lot of HAL, the space ship's board computer of Kubrick's "Space Odyssey": Both are fitted out with artificial intelligence and go rogue. <br/><br/>Incarceron takes place in the future. 160 years ago a king decided that cutting off mankind from its strive after one technological improvement after the next would end greed, war and the slow crumbling of society. So he forbid time and progress and switched everything back to an era long passed: An age, when people traveled o</span>
  <span id="freeText3389586978076639844" style="display:none">The prison Incarceron reminds me a lot of HAL, the space ship's board computer of Kubrick's "Space Odyssey": Both are fitted out with artificial intelligence and go rogue. <br /><br />Incarceron takes place in the future. 160 years ago a king decided that cutting off mankind from its strive after one technological improvement after the next would end greed, war and the slow crumbling of society. So he forbid time and progress and switched everything back to an era long passed: An age, when people traveled on horseback and did without electricity. But the same new old era also contains computer generated old-looking trees and fake spiderwebs - and rich people have found ways to hide electric cables in the staff rooms and lush bathrooms behind secret panels. Following the so-called "Protocol" completely is only obligatory if you are lower class.<br /><br />A second step towards a violence and crime-free world was the construction of the self-regulating, autonomous prison Incarceron, where all criminal, dangerous, politically extreme and mentally ill people were sent off to - together with 70 volunteers to guard them. The fact that after closing the doors nobody could enter and nobody could leave played into the hands of Incarceron itself: Nobody could hinder it to turn the planned paradise into a hell serving it's own strange taste in amusement. Not even the learned volunteers.<br /><br />In the real world nobody knows about the unpleasant development of the former experiment. Nobody but the Warden, who has got the only key to the prison. <br /><br />The story follows Claudia, the present Warden's daughter, who has been promised to the unfit Crown Prince to be his future bride, on the "Outside" and gang member Finn, who woke up inside the prison at the age of fifteen without a proper memory, on the "Inside". He claims not to be one of the prison's recycled products, but to be imported from the real world - where he wants to return to.<br /><br />Also lined up are a handful of interesting side-characters including Claudia's tutor Jared, the ice-cold and scheming Warden and the evil Queen on the one side, and Keiro, Finn's oathbrother and two other travel-mates (Gildas and Attia) on the other side.<br /><br />The story kept my attention all of the time. I liked Finn a lot and Claudia a little less. In fact, she was sometimes quite annoying, which can be explained by her upbringing as the next puppet on the throne. But I always wanted to know what happened next - even to her.<br /><br />The plot ends with a cliff-hanger. But the sequel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4499214.Sapphique" rel="nofollow noopener">Sapphique</a> is already available.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3389586978076639844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3456959300" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3456959300" />
    <a title="Elizabeth Ross" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/116889360-elizabeth-ross"><img alt="Elizabeth Ross" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592206059p2/116889360.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3456959300?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth Ross" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth Ross" href="/user/show/116889360-elizabeth-ross">Elizabeth Ross</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116889360-elizabeth-ross?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3456959300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5161284501373599750"><i>
  <b>"Only the man who knows freedom can define his prison."</b>
</i><br/><br/> Do you know those blurbs that sound really interesting and make you really curious about a story, just for you to end up disappointed when you actually read the story itself? That's <i>Incarceron</i>'s blurb. And yes, I've already find blurbs more interesting than this one, but still. It was intriguing and I was curious to read the story. But then I read it and I wish I hadn't.<br/><br/> Let's start with the plot. It is so freaking dull I am surprised I</span>
  <span id="freeText5161284501373599750" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"Only the man who knows freedom can define his prison."</b>
</i><br /><br /> Do you know those blurbs that sound really interesting and make you really curious about a story, just for you to end up disappointed when you actually read the story itself? That's <i>Incarceron</i>'s blurb. And yes, I've already find blurbs more interesting than this one, but still. It was intriguing and I was curious to read the story. But then I read it and I wish I hadn't.<br /><br /> Let's start with the plot. It is so freaking dull I am surprised I didn't fall asleep. Finn's parts (being Finn a prisoner of Incarceron, a giant prison that is alive and whose location is known only by the Warden) should have been full of action and really interesting to read, because after all they are trying to survive in a place full of thieves and assassins where there's no rules, but the action that actually exists is definitely not enough to catch my attention for more than a few pages (and by few I mean one, two pages). And then we have Claudia's parts (being Claudia a lady from the the real world where development was forbidden and everyone lives like they were still in the XVI century). It seemed to be promissing me some political trama to make up for the lack of action, but I didn't get any! So it was basically me reading about a spoiled girl who doesn't want to marry and therefore creates an overcomplicated plan that makes no sense at all.<br /><br /> Which leads me to the fact that this plot has more holes than a Swees cheese. Claudia's overcomplicated plan, for example. Close your eyes and imagine that you are a lady in the XVI century, meant to marry the future king, and you don't want to. What do you do? A) Run away. B) Try to find a reasonable way of getting off the marriage. C) Waste all the time you have to prepare yourself for option A) or B) trying to find a way to prove to the world that the dead Heir Prince is alive, even if you have no proof of that and everyone believes he is dead. Guess which option she chose? If you said option C) you are 100% freaking right. Now tell me, who in his/her right mind would try to do something like that?! I mean, c'mon. You may hope he is alive and want to try to find him, but at least have some sort of plan B) just in case you can't find anything. But oh, wait! This is fiction, so of course Claudia's unreliable and overcomplicated plan will work. <br /><br /> Then we have the whole thing of the Heir Prince being alive. Because the Queen wants him gone, so her own son can get the crown, but instead of killing him, she sends him to Incarceron, even if she is clearly fine with killing people. Okay, right. It obviously makes sense. But then again, it is fiction and if the Prince had been killed, Fisher would have no plot to work with, so of course he needed to go to Incarceron. 🙄<br /><br /> And you don't need to be a genius to guess who our Heir Prince is, do you? Yes, it is that obvious. And was obvious since the moment the whole dead/disappeared Heir Prince thing is mentioned. To be fair, though, Fisher made no effort to hide that fact, so I really don't know if she wanted the revelation to be a twist or not. What I do know is that it made me even more irritated with the plot.<br /><br /> But then, I reached the end of the book. And was completly blown away by a series of unpredictable plot twists, that caught me completly off guard, because I really didn't think Fisher would be able to surprise me, and made me not only love the end but want the next book. WHY DO AUTHORD NEED TO MAKE BOOKS LIKE THIS?! I mean, WHY? Why can't I have an amazing book from the beginning till the end, so I can finish it and say without doubts that I <i>
  <b>want</b>
</i> the next one? Why making me end it with this bittersweet feeling, wanting the next book, but fearing that it might be as dull as the first?!<br /><br /> If only being dull was the only problem of the story! But it isn't. The characters are terrible. Flat and one dimensional. Claudia got in my nerves as I don't remember any character to do. Stupid little spoiled brat! I mean, she doesn't even really care about Finn, she only wants a way to get away from that stupid marriage. She is a spoiled girl throwing a tantrum. Period. Finn is well... I don't know. I can't even remember what he is supposed to look like. Personality traits? That I can remember, none either. All I can say is that in that dark world of Incarceron, he is the special guy. And it's basically that. Then we have sidekicks/friends that somehow could receive even less development than Claudia and Finn did. I can't even remember their names, sorry. The Queen and Claudia's father are evil. Because we need evil characters. And that's everything they are. It seems that being evil is a full-time personality trait and it's enough to describe a character... 🤷‍♀️<br /><br /> The only character I could actually like is a sidekick and somehow (and luckly) escaped from that group I referred and that got even less development than Claudia and Finn. He is Finn's best friend/brother-in-arms. The only character that actually got some personality traits I can remember. He is charismatic, cocky and a little crazy. Truth be told, I have a thing for this kind of characters, but still. It is hard for you to do not like Keiro when he is the only character with a personality. <br /><br /> Sadly, not even the world can escape my rant. I loved the idea. 100% loved it. Fine, whoever thought it would actually work was stupid beyond belief. It's not like the XVI century was a bed of roses where everyone was happy all the time. And of course no one can ever create a paradise, fill it with people and expect it to remain a paradise. People are not perfect and do not fit in a perfect world. But hell, the damn idea was amazing! I loved it and I don't mind to keep saying that. And I have nothing bad to say about Incarceron. It is just perfect. The whole live prison idea as well as its completly original location are absolutely amazing. But the real world part could have been so much better executed. It left me so many questions. I mean, technology is not allowed but the whole Warden's house is filled with it, to make sure everything looks like they live in a XVI century house. The Queen has a freaking elevator. And new things keep being created, even if they can't be used. I get the idea of Fisher wanting us to see that the idea of that idiot doesn't work at all and that humans can't live without technology nowadays. But my mind can't add all those rules broken by the ones who should want them to be followed and the world Fisher wanted to create. It just made me so confused during almost the whole book that I couldn't really appreciate the world as much as I wanted to.<br /><br /> Overall, I can't actually see why so many people like this book. I won't deny that the world is genial, it definitely is, but the actual story is definitely not that good. I can't really say that I recommed this book, even though I LOVED those plot twists at the end, which makes me quite sad. And honestly, despite having it in my TBR list, I don't really know if I am going to give the next book a try. I am too scared of getting disappointed. <br /> <br /><i>
  <b>"Despair is deep. An abyss that shallows dreams."</b>
</i><br /><br /><u>SCORE: 1.75 out of 5.00 stars</u><br /><br />You can also find this review on my <a href="https://bookwormslittlespot.wordpress.com/2020/07/27/incarceron/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5161284501373599750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/820737-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299297815p2/820737.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122999793?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/820737-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Capa dura 9780803733961" href="/book/show/6727322-incarceron">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122999793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2087566614922401938">I wish I could give half-stars, because this is really 3 1/2. <br/><br/>I thought the ideas in this book were rich and innovative, and the plot twists near the end were what made me round the rating up to 4 stars instead of rounding down. I definitely want to read the sequel to find out where this story goes. (Update: I recently moved my rating down to 3 stars because as time has gone by I stopped caring about reading the sequel! Just didn't resonate with me, I guess.)<br/><br/>The big negative for me was that this</span>
  <span id="freeText2087566614922401938" style="display:none">I wish I could give half-stars, because this is really 3 1/2. <br /><br />I thought the ideas in this book were rich and innovative, and the plot twists near the end were what made me round the rating up to 4 stars instead of rounding down. I definitely want to read the sequel to find out where this story goes. (Update: I recently moved my rating down to 3 stars because as time has gone by I stopped caring about reading the sequel! Just didn't resonate with me, I guess.)<br /><br />The big negative for me was that this author loves trying to make her writing sound pretty, and in doing that she leaves too many details out to the point where I was like, "What the heck is going on?" Especially in a fantasy where everything is made-up, I could have used a little more meat and potatoes in the descriptions (and that's coming from a "less descriptions, more dialogue" sort of girl). Also, this author apparently likes to write poetry, which makes sense because there are some parts that are cheesier than my kid's dairy drawer in the fridge. Not that the plot itself is cheesy, just the way she structures her sentences. <br /><br />Oh, and she is a heavy user of the "B" word. Maybe that's not considered a bad word in England? 'Cause I think this author's British.</span>

<div id="review_909991360" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/909991360" />
    <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light"><img alt="Crystal Starr Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573066911p2/3990525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/909991360?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal Starr Light" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780307707079" href="/book/show/7058934-incarceron">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=2014-owned-challenge">2014-owned-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=so-boring-it-s-boring">so-boring-it-s-boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=big-heap-of-meh">big-heap-of-meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=it-s-not-you-it-s-me">it-s-not-you-it-s-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer909991360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17734389747309055213">Bullet Review:<br/><br/>If there is one thing I've learned over the years, it's that life is too short to spend on books and things that you aren't enjoying.<br/><br/>DNF @ 19%.<br/><br/>Some people will love "Incarceron". Hell, lots of my friends already do. And I can understand why - it's a pretty unique concept and (so far) doesn't rely 100% on insta-love, romantic plot triangles, and stupid characters. And for people who love steampunk, there's that as well.<br/><br/>But, it really doesn't have the things I like to read in a book.</span>
  <span id="freeText17734389747309055213" style="display:none">Bullet Review:<br /><br />If there is one thing I've learned over the years, it's that life is too short to spend on books and things that you aren't enjoying.<br /><br />DNF @ 19%.<br /><br />Some people will love "Incarceron". Hell, lots of my friends already do. And I can understand why - it's a pretty unique concept and (so far) doesn't rely 100% on insta-love, romantic plot triangles, and stupid characters. And for people who love steampunk, there's that as well.<br /><br />But, it really doesn't have the things I like to read in a book. The characters are dull and hard to root for. Claudia, our female viewpoint character, has a plotline related to her being betrothed to royal d-bag, Casper. The Queen is evil. The setting is faux steampunk, and I'm no steampunk fan. And more importantly, the world-building is CONFUSING and hard to follow and BORING. I'm not quite sure what the plot is other than "Incarceron and the Queen are evil! We must defeat them!" - and I can't tell you how many times I've seen THAT plot variation.<br /><br />Great idea, badly executed, but hey, there's a lot worse out there, which is why I'm rating 3 rather than 2 stars. Plus, a book that DOESN'T feature our female viewpoint character immediately getting wet panties over a boy is worth recommending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17734389747309055213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142418529" href="/book/show/9025022-incarceron">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66639925-amber-j?shelf=2020-reading-challenge">2020-reading-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3329080971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9411587568009534807"><i>I try to express only my most honest opinion in a spoiler-free way. Unfortunately, there is still always a risk of slight spoilers despite my best efforts. If you feel something in my review is a spoiler please let me know. Thank you.</i><br/><br/>So I really wanted to give this book a 4 star, but after three-fourths of this book being 2.5 stars and only the last fourth being amazing, I just couldn't justify such a high rating. This book took a really long time to get into. I considered not finishing it more </span>
  <span id="freeText9411587568009534807" style="display:none"><i>I try to express only my most honest opinion in a spoiler-free way. Unfortunately, there is still always a risk of slight spoilers despite my best efforts. If you feel something in my review is a spoiler please let me know. Thank you.</i><br /><br />So I really wanted to give this book a 4 star, but after three-fourths of this book being 2.5 stars and only the last fourth being amazing, I just couldn't justify such a high rating. This book took a really long time to get into. I considered not finishing it more than once and forced myself through the first 300 pages at least. The ending was good though and I found that I couldn't put it down near the end. <br /><br />The characters in this book are crazy. I love them. Even the two main characters are flawed and not the perfect images of morality that normally come with the heroes/heroines of a story, and the side characters had a lot going on. I was bouncing between hating and loving them. Except for Jared, he is definitely a character meant to be liked. And Keiro, he really grates on my nerves. I don't think I like him at all. <br /><br />After that ending, I'm thinking (hoping) that the second book will be much better than the first. Part of this book's problem is you didn't know what was going on. I think the author was going for mysterious and plot twists, but most of the time it was just confusing and highly annoying. And it never did fully explain the Era thing and why they did that. They explain it some, but not enough to my satisfaction. <br /><br />All in all, I think the book is worth the read. Not 'the best fantasy book ever written' like the review on the cover said, but still worth reading, and I will be finishing the series. I have high hopes it won't take as long to get into.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_134404770" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134404770" />
    <a title="Eileen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3650310-eileen"><img alt="Eileen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1322429351p2/3650310.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134404770?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eileen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eileen" href="/user/show/3650310-eileen">Eileen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142418529" href="/book/show/9025022-incarceron">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3650310-eileen?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134404770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3714550192932018145">I thoroughly enjoyed reading this, but I have always been into reading fairytales and although they don't live happily ever after, this book reads like a fairytale. It's a very imaginative, original and engrossing story that is vividly written with great characters. It has action and suspense, but no romance (thank God, no love-triangle!).I loved every second of it and although I didn't want to rush through it and enjoy it to the fullest, I couldn't put it down until I reached the last page. It'</span>
  <span id="freeText3714550192932018145" style="display:none">I thoroughly enjoyed reading this, but I have always been into reading fairytales and although they don't live happily ever after, this book reads like a fairytale. It's a very imaginative, original and engrossing story that is vividly written with great characters. It has action and suspense, but no romance (thank God, no love-triangle!).I loved every second of it and although I didn't want to rush through it and enjoy it to the fullest, I couldn't put it down until I reached the last page. It's all about Finn, Claudia and of course Incarceron.<br /><br />Finn is a prisoner with no memory, sure he came from Outside though the prison has been sealed for centuries and only one man has ever escaped. More than anything he wants to know who he is and where he came from, but can he ever be sure? He hates it that he has no choice, but to leave his friends behind on the Inside.<br /><br />Claudia, the daughter of the Warden of Incarceron, lives Outside like a prisoner in a manor house, in a society where time is forbidden and doomed to an arranged marriage. She unravels the mystery around the death of a Prince, she thinks she knows the truth and she thinks that she knows who she is, but does she really?<br /><br />Finn and Claudia both want to escape, they both hold a key and they both want to KNOW. They meet, bond and are united in their fight for freedom and truth.<br /><br />Incarceron is alive, sees and hears everything and is, like Finn and Claudia, also looking for a way out.<br /><br />Can't wait to read the sequel: "Sapphique".<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3714550192932018145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_469061754" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/469061754" />
    <a title="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer"><img alt="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553042105p2/7476091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/469061754?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" href="/user/show/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer">Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=genre-dystopian">genre-dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=stars-3-5">stars-3-5</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=imo-monsters-unique">imo-monsters-unique</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=g-t-historical">g-t-historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=genre-friendship">genre-friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=series-book-1">series-book-1</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=genre-steampunk">genre-steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=review-wrote-add-later">review-wrote-add-later</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=imo-sequel-i-think-not">imo-sequel-i-think-not</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer469061754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17703073190705823343"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513291717i/24679810._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='279' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><i>Check out more reviews @ <a href='https://perspectiveofawriter.wordpress.com/book-reviews/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Perspective of a Writer</a>...</i><br/><br/>Incarceron is a futuristic prison, a living building where the descendants of the original prisoners live in a dark world… A young prisoner, Finn, has visions of an earlier life, and can’t believe he has always been there. Claudia, the Warden’s daughter, finds a crystal key, through which she can talk to Finn and he her… and with that a plan of escape is born…<br/><br/><br/><b>The short review...</b><br/><br/>The premise is pretty rockin' ... I liked the sound of it from the </span>
  <span id="freeText17703073190705823343" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513291717i/24679810._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="279" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><i>Check out more reviews @ <a href="https://perspectiveofawriter.wordpress.com/book-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Perspective of a Writer</a>...</i><br><br>Incarceron is a futuristic prison, a living building where the descendants of the original prisoners live in a dark world… A young prisoner, Finn, has visions of an earlier life, and can’t believe he has always been there. Claudia, the Warden’s daughter, finds a crystal key, through which she can talk to Finn and he her… and with that a plan of escape is born…<br><br><br><b>The short review...</b><br><br>The premise is pretty rockin' ... I liked the sound of it from the beginning and it lasted on my TBR for all these years because it still appealed to me every time I read it. Plus every once in a while I'd read a rave review. I still enjoyed how the premise played out and actually suggest anyone who LOVES characters and plot twists to read this book... It pretty much is a stand alone although there is a second book that makes a duology. So those are the strengths... characters worth following, twists galore and could be read as a standalone dystopian steampunk.<br><br>So why the 3 stars?! Well, while I quite enjoyed the characters (every single one of them from the 2 protagonists, to the villains and all the friends) the plot did NOT measure up. The book premise almost tells you TOO much there is so little plot. Individual interactions along the journey from point A to point B were decent at times but came to nothing and in the end was a convoluted mess for no reason. In fact, the villains could have been disposed of easily and the warden's plan could have been executed flawlessly, his aims achieved. And his actions in the end were puzzling as they quite randomly provided a reason for a second book rather than ending this book at a really good place.<br><br><br><b>Cover &amp; Title grade -&gt; Original-&gt;C- Reprint-&gt;B+</b><br><br>I chose the later cover because the aesthetics just work to showcase the story MUCH better than the original cover. In fact, if I'd seen the original cover first I probably would never have put it on my TBR... The blue-black color and the gears background do speak toward a steampunk world... especially one where there is a lot of decay and faux vegetation. The only problem is the key... If you are going to use such a distinctive item then please give the illustrator the worded description to work from! It just doesn't look like a key that has secret buttons and is super high tech...<br><br><br><b>Who are these characters worth following?</b><br><br>-The Protagonists!<br>Told is a dual narrative, we follow Finn, inside the prison as he has strange dreams that feel like memories and Claudia, a girl determined to flout her father's royal aims for her. While I didn't feel like Claudia had any motivation to oppose her father, I quite liked her. She was quick thinking, bold and determined. Finn was a more desperate figure who tried to retain his moral ground while the prison and its occupants did everything to cause him to give way. They contrasted each other quite well and made it easy for me to finish reading (it wasn't a drag at all!)<br><br>-The Villains!<br>We have a plethora of villains... Incarceron itself, Blaze, a mysteriously scarred man, the Warden, and the Queen as well as Claudia's fiancee and possibly a court official who could be playing sides. Finn and Claudia and their friends are up against A LOT! Besides the history of Incarceron being lost to time with all of its pertinent physical details there are those power games that come with court intrigue. And Claudia doesn't want to hate her father even as she understands she must oppose him. Incarceron though was the most intriguing with its mental health crisis due to playing god for so long a time...<br><br>-The Friends!<br>The friends of a story can really be a toss up to making a book readable to me or not. And these friends do their job! Claudia has Julian, a scholar of some brilliance. Finn has an old scholar, Gildas who trusts in Finn's visions, his blood oath brother, Keiro and a girl, Attia. Attia was my favorite but I loved all of these guys... within Incarceron you really don't know who will or won't betray you... so I was worried the entire time about who Finn trusted... And Claudia could have Julian ripped away at any time!! I won't say a double cross isn't possible, because up until the betrayal friends are still friends...right?!<br><br><br><b>As a Writer...</b><br><br>This is one of those times when a premise told too much and pretty much tanked the book for the reader. Not that the plot couldn't also be improved but with less information I could have gone in not expecting MORE on top of the premise. (Which come on, admit it... We ALL want the premise to be talking about the setup, and account for maybe 25-30% of the book... not ALL 100% of it.)<br><br>As a writer myself, plot is soooo important to me. I don't want readers to see what is coming clearly and easily... that is too much and will ruin a story. Instead play to the characters strengths and weaknesses... pit their desires against one another... internal conflict is just as powerful a plot element as physical danger and twists...<br><br>Incarceron's plot is pretty basic and brought down a well characterized and developed world. It's not perfect but if characters are your jam then this is the read for you... Follow them as they plunge through the creepy world of the prison of Incarceron.<br><br>⋆ ⭐⭐⭐⭐ Authenticity<br>⋆ ⭐⭐⭐⭐ Writing Style<br>⋆ ⋆ ⋆ ⭐⭐ Plot &amp; Pacing<br>⋆ ⭐⭐⭐⭐ World Building<br><br>BOTTOM LINE: Characters worth traveling through Incarceron for...<br><br>______________________<br>You can find this review and many others on my book blog @ <a href="https://perspectiveofawriter.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Perspective of a Writer</a>. See my special perspective at the bottom of my reviews under the typewriter...</span>
  <a data-text-id="17703073190705823343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yj1knUs8BFwGfA89aW93PXeMwhxywCPlVXLKzRUbuHfeUr4NUw68n+fnelCYM+E8Dt50T+MBgv0QKB4EeyG5RA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7VIWHZgMtSrHznYmDHmO5b8S1Yp1LrulboNb9H/AmWf5PcyNgD4N6SZVA0v9JRjkxkBj2eTvGr0r2Y89EfqYVA==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/190887.Catherine_Fisher">About Catherine Fisher</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/190887.Catherine_Fisher"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1309461768p3/190887.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/190887.Catherine_Fisher">Catherine Fisher
</a></div>

1,512
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4022463802686885461">Catherine Fisher was born in Newport, Wales. She graduated from the University of Wales with a degree in English and a fascination for myth and history. She has worked in education and archaeology and as a lecturer in creative writing at the University of Glamorgan. She is a Fellow of the Welsh Academy.<br/><br/>Catherine is an acclaimed poet and novelist, regularly lecturing and giving readings to groups o</span>
  <span id="freeText4022463802686885461" style="display:none">Catherine Fisher was born in Newport, Wales. She graduated from the University of Wales with a degree in English and a fascination for myth and history. She has worked in education and archaeology and as a lecturer in creative writing at the University of Glamorgan. She is a Fellow of the Welsh Academy.<br /><br />Catherine is an acclaimed poet and novelist, regularly lecturing and giving readings to groups of all ages. She leads sessions for teachers and librarians and is an experienced broadcaster and adjudicator. She lives in Newport, Gwent.<br /><br />Catherine has won many awards and much critical acclaim for her work. Her poetry has appeared in leading periodicals and anthologies and her volume Immrama won the WAC Young Writers' Prize. She won the Cardiff International Poetry Competition in 1990.<br /><br />Her first novel, The Conjuror's Game, was shortlisted for the Smarties Books prize and The Snow-Walker's Son for the W.H.Smith Award. Equally acclaimed is her quartet The Book of the Crow, a classic of fantasy fiction.<br /><br />The Oracle, the first volume in the Oracle trilogy, blends Egyptian and Greek elements of magic and adventure and was shortlisted for the Whitbread Children's Books prize. The trilogy was an international bestseller and has appeared in over twenty languages. The Candleman won the Welsh Books Council's Tir Na n'Og Prize and Catherine was also shortlisted for the remarkable Corbenic, a modern re-inventing of the Grail legend.<br /><br />Her futuristic novel Incarceron was published to widespread praise in 2007, winning the Mythopoeic Society of America's Children's Fiction Award and selected by The Times as its Children's Book of the Year. The sequel, Sapphique, was published in September 2008.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4022463802686885461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
